  {
    title: 'CVE-2022-50650 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'bpf Fix reference state manage...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2022-50650',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 09 Dec 2025 01:16:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'bpf Fix reference state management for synchronous callbacks\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Currently, verifier verifies callback functions (sync and async) as if\r\n' +
      'they will be executed once, (i.e. it explores execution state as if the\r\n' +
      'function was being called once). The next insn to explore is set to\r\n' +
      'start of subprog and the exit from nested frame is handled using\r\n' +
      'curframe > 0 and prepare_func_exit. In case of async callback it uses a\r\n' +
      'customized variant of push_stack simulating a kind of branch to set up\r\n' +
      'custom state and execution context for the async callback.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'While this approach is simple and works when callback really will be\r\n' +
      'executed only once, it is unsafe for all of our current helpers which\r\n' +
      'are for_each style, i.e. they execute the callback multiple times.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'A callback releasing acquired references of the caller may do so\r\n' +
      'multiple times, but currently verifier sees it as one call inside the\r\n' +
      'frame, which then returns to caller. Hence, it thinks it released some\r\n' +
      'reference that the cb e.g. got access through callback_ctx (register\r\n' +
      'filled inside cb from spilled typed register on stack).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Similarly, it may see that an acquire call is unpaired inside the\r\n' +
      'callback, so the caller will copy the reference state of callback and\r\n' +
      'then will have to release the register with new ref_obj_ids. But again,\r\n' +
      'the callback may execute multiple times, but the verifier will only\r\n' +
      'account for acquired references for a single symbolic execution of the\r\n' +
      'callback, which will cause leaks.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Note that for async callback case, things are different. While currently\r\n' +
      'we have bpf_timer_set_callback which only executes it once, even for\r\n' +
      'multiple executions it would be safe, as reference state is NULL and\r\n' +
      'check_reference_leak would force program to release state before\r\n' +
      'BPF_EXIT. The state is also unaffected by analysis for the caller frame.\r\n' +
      'Hence async callback is safe.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Since we want the reference state to be accessible, e.g. for pointers\r\n' +
      "loaded from stack through callback_ctx's PTR_TO_STACK, we still have to\r\n" +
      "copy caller's reference_state to callback's bpf_func_state, but we\r\n" +
      'enforce that whatever references it adds to that reference_state has\r\n' +
      'been released before it hits BPF_EXIT. This requires introducing a new\r\n' +
      'callback_ref member in the reference state to distinguish between caller\r\n' +
      'vs callee references. Hence, check_reference_leak now errors out if it\r\n' +
      'sees we are in callback_fn and we have not released callback_ref refs.\r\n' +
      'Since there can be multiple nested callbacks, like frame 0 -> cb1 -> cb2\r\n' +
      'etc. we need to also distinguish between whether this particular ref\r\n' +
      'belongs to this callback frame or parent, and only error for our own, so\r\n' +
      'we store state->frameno (which is always non-zero for callbacks).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'In short, callbacks can read parent reference_state, but cannot mutate\r\n' +
      'it, to be able to use pointers acquired by the caller. They must only\r\n' +
      'undo their changes (by releasing their own acquired_refs before\r\n' +
      'BPF_EXIT) on top of caller reference_state before returning (at which\r\n' +
      'point the caller and callback state will match anyway, so no need to\r\n' +
      'copy it back to caller). | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>',
    contentSnippet: '![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'bpf Fix reference state management for synchronous callbacks\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Currently, verifier verifies callback functions (sync and async) as if\r\n' +
      'they will be executed once, (i.e. it explores execution state as if the\r\n' +
      'function was being called once). The next insn to explore is set to\r\n' +
      'start of subprog and the exit from nested frame is handled using\r\n' +
      'curframe > 0 and prepare_func_exit. In case of async callback it uses a\r\n' +
      'customized variant of push_stack simulating a kind of branch to set up\r\n' +
      'custom state and execution context for the async callback.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'While this approach is simple and works when callback really will be\r\n' +
      'executed only once, it is unsafe for all of our current helpers which\r\n' +
      'are for_each style, i.e. they execute the callback multiple times.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'A callback releasing acquired references of the caller may do so\r\n' +
      'multiple times, but currently verifier sees it as one call inside the\r\n' +
      'frame, which then returns to caller. Hence, it thinks it released some\r\n' +
      'reference that the cb e.g. got access through callback_ctx (register\r\n' +
      'filled inside cb from spilled typed register on stack).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Similarly, it may see that an acquire call is unpaired inside the\r\n' +
      'callback, so the caller will copy the reference state of callback and\r\n' +
      'then will have to release the register with new ref_obj_ids. But again,\r\n' +
      'the callback may execute multiple times, but the verifier will only\r\n' +
      'account for acquired references for a single symbolic execution of the\r\n' +
      'callback, which will cause leaks.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Note that for async callback case, things are different. While currently\r\n' +
      'we have bpf_timer_set_callback which only executes it once, even for\r\n' +
      'multiple executions it would be safe, as reference state is NULL and\r\n' +
      'check_reference_leak would force program to release state before\r\n' +
      'BPF_EXIT. The state is also unaffected by analysis for the caller frame.\r\n' +
      'Hence async callback is safe.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Since we want the reference state to be accessible, e.g. for pointers\r\n' +
      "loaded from stack through callback_ctx's PTR_TO_STACK, we still have to\r\n" +
      "copy caller's reference_state to callback's bpf_func_state, but we\r\n" +
      'enforce that whatever references it adds to that reference_state has\r\n' +
      'been released before it hits BPF_EXIT. This requires introducing a new\r\n' +
      'callback_ref member in the reference state to distinguish between caller\r\n' +
      'vs callee references. Hence, check_reference_leak now errors out if it\r\n' +
      'sees we are in callback_fn and we have not released callback_ref refs.\r\n' +
      'Since there can be multiple nested callbacks, like frame 0 -> cb1 -> cb2\r\n' +
      'etc. we need to also distinguish between whether this particular ref\r\n' +
      'belongs to this callback frame or parent, and only error for our own, so\r\n' +
      'we store state->frameno (which is always non-zero for callbacks).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'In short, callbacks can read parent reference_state, but cannot mutate\r\n' +
      'it, to be able to use pointers acquired by the caller. They must only\r\n' +
      'undo their changes (by releasing their own acquired_refs before\r\n' +
      'BPF_EXIT) on top of caller reference_state before returning (at which\r\n' +
      'point the caller and callback state will match anyway, so no need to\r\n' +
      'copy it back to caller). | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>',

    title: 'CVE-2023-53777 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +

    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2023-53777',

    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'erofs kill hooked chains to avoid loops on deduplicated compressed images\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'After heavily stressing EROFS with several images which include a\r\n' +
      'hand-crafted image of repeated patterns for more than 46 days, I found\r\n' +
      'two chains could be linked with each other almost simultaneously and\r\n' +
      "form a loop so that the entire loop won't be submitted.  As a\r\n" +
      'consequence, the corresponding file pages will remain locked forever.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'It can be _only_ observed on data-deduplicated compressed images.\r\n' +
      'For example, consider two chains with five pclusters in total\r\n' +
      '\tChain 1  2->3->4->5    -- The tail pcluster is 5\r\n' +
      '        Chain 2  5->1->2       -- The tail pcluster is 2.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Chain 2 could link to Chain 1 with pcluster 5 and Chain 1 could link\r\n' +
      'to Chain 2 at the same time with pcluster 2.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Since hooked chains are all linked locklessly now, I have no idea how\r\n' +
      "to simply avoid the race.  Instead, let's avoid hooked chains completely\r\n" +
      'until I could work out a proper way to fix this and end users finally\r\n' +
      "tell us that it's needed to add it back.\r\n" +
      '\r\n' +
      'Actually, this optimization can be found with multi-threaded workloads\r\n' +
      "(especially even more often on deduplicated compressed images), yet I'm\r\n" +
      'not sure about the overall system impacts of not having this compared\r\n' +
      'with implementation complexity. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>',

  {
    title: 'CVE-2023-53778 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'accel/qaic Clean up integer ov...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2023-53778',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 09 Dec 2025 01:16:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'accel/qaic Clean up integer overflow checking in map_user_pages()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The encode_dma() function has some validation on in_trans->size but it\r\n' +
      'would be more clear to move those checks to find_and_map_user_pages().\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The encode_dma() had two checks\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '\tif (in_trans->addr + in_trans->size  in_trans->addr || !in_trans->size)\r\n' +
      '\t\treturn -EINVAL\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The in_trans->addr variable is the starting address.  The in_trans->size\r\n' +
      'variable is the total size of the transfer.  The transfer can occur in\r\n' +
      'parts and the resources->xferred_dma_size tracks how many bytes we have\r\n' +
      'already transferred.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This patch introduces a new variable "remaining" which represents the\r\n' +
      'amount we want to transfer (in_trans->size) minus the amount we have\r\n' +
      'already transferred (resources->xferred_dma_size).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'I have modified the check for if in_trans->size is zero to instead check\r\n' +
      'if in_trans->size is less than resources->xferred_dma_size.  If we have\r\n' +
      'already transferred more bytes than in_trans->size then there are negative\r\n' +
      "bytes remaining which doesn't make sense.  If there are zero bytes\r\n" +
      'remaining to be copied, just return success.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The check in encode_dma() checked that "addr + size" could not overflow\r\n' +
      "and barring a driver bug that should work, but it's easier to check if\r\n" +
      'we do this in parts.  First check that "in_trans->addr +\r\n' +
      'resources->xferred_dma_size" is safe.  Then check that "xfer_start_addr +\r\n' +
      'remaining" is safe.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'My final concern was that we are dealing with u64 values but on 32bit\r\n' +
      'systems the kmalloc() function will truncate the sizes to 32 bits.  So\r\n' +
      'I calculated "total = in_trans->size + offset_in_page(xfer_start_addr)"\r\n' +
      'and returned -EINVAL if it were >= SIZE_MAX.  This will not affect 64bit\r\n' +
      'systems. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>',

      '\r\n' +
      'The in_trans->addr variable is the starting address.  The in_trans->size\r\n' +
      'variable is the total size of the transfer.  The transfer can occur in\r\n' +
      'parts and the resources->xferred_dma_size tracks how many bytes we have\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'I have modified the check for if in_trans->size is zero to instead check\r\n' +
      'if in_trans->size is less than resources->xferred_dma_size.  If we have\r\n' +
      'already transferred more bytes than in_trans->size then there are negative\r\n' +
      "bytes remaining which doesn't make sense.  If there are zero bytes\r\n" +
      'remaining to be copied, just return success.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The check in encode_dma() checked that "addr + size" could not overflow\r\n' +
      "and barring a driver bug that should work, but it's easier to check if\r\n" +
      'we do this in parts.  First check that "in_trans->addr +\r\n' +
      'resources->xferred_dma_size" is safe.  Then check that "xfer_start_addr +\r\n' +
      'remaining" is safe.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'My final concern was that we are dealing with u64 values but on 32bit\r\n' +
      'systems the kmalloc() function will truncate the sizes to 32 bits.  So\r\n' +
      'I calculated "total = in_trans->size + offset_in_page(xfer_start_addr)"\r\n' +
      'and returned -EINVAL if it were >= SIZE_MAX.  This will not affect 64bit\r\n' +
      'systems. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>',

    title: 'CVE-2023-53785 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "mt76 mt7921 don't assume adeq...",
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2023-53785',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 09 Dec 2025 01:16:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "mt76 mt7921 don't assume adequate headroom for SDIO headers\r\n" +
      '\r\n' +
      'mt7921_usb_sdio_tx_prepare_skb() calls mt7921_usb_sdio_write_txwi() and\r\n' +
      'mt7921_skb_add_usb_sdio_hdr(), both of which blindly assume that\r\n' +
      'adequate headroom will be available in the passed skb. This assumption\r\n' +
      'typically is satisfied when the skb was allocated in the net core for\r\n' +
      'transmission via the mt7921 netdev (although even that is only an\r\n' +
      'optimization and is not strictly guaranteed), but the assumption is\r\n' +
      'sometimes not satisfied when the skb originated in the receive path of\r\n' +
      'another netdev and was passed through to the mt7921, such as by the\r\n' +
      'bridge layer. Blindly prepending bytes to an skb is always wrong.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This commit introduces a call to skb_cow_head() before the call to\r\n' +
      'mt7921_usb_sdio_write_txwi() in mt7921_usb_sdio_tx_prepare_skb() to\r\n' +
      'ensure that at least MT_SDIO_TXD_SIZE + MT_SDIO_HDR_SIZE bytes can be\r\n' +
      'pushed onto the skb.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Without this fix, I can trivially cause kernel panics by bridging an\r\n' +
      'MT7921AU-based USB 802.11ax interface with an Ethernet interface on an\r\n' +
      'Intel Atom-based x86 system using its onboard RTL8169 PCI Ethernet\r\n' +
      'adapter and also on an ARM-based Raspberry Pi 1 using its onboard\r\n' +
      'SMSC9512 USB Ethernet adapter. Note that the panics do not occur in\r\n' +
      'every system configuration, as they occur only if the receiving netdev\r\n' +
      'leaves less headroom in its received skbs than the mt7921 needs for its\r\n' +
      'SDIO headers.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Here is an example stack trace of this panic on Raspberry Pi OS Lite\r\n' +
      '2023-02-21 running kernel 6.1.24+ [1]\r\n' +

      ' kthread from ret_from_fork+0x14/0x34\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'iommufd IOMMUFD_DESTROY should not increase the refcount\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +

      '       if (IS_ERR(obj))\r\n' +

      '       iommufd_ref_to_users(obj)\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'Allowing the refcount the be elevated without holding the destroy_rwsem\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'ethtool Fix uninitialized number of lanes\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'It is not possible to set the number of lanes when setting link modes\r\n' +
      "using the legacy IOCTL ethtool interface. Since 'struct\r\n" +
      "ethtool_link_ksettings' is not initialized in this path, drivers receive\r\n" +
      "an uninitialized number of lanes in 'struct\r\n" +
      "ethtool_link_ksettingslanes'.\r\n" +
      '\r\n' +
      'When this information is later queried from drivers, it results in the\r\n' +
      'ethtool code making decisions based on uninitialized memory, leading to\r\n' +
      'the following KMSAN splat [1]. In practice, this most likely only\r\n' +

    title: 'CVE-2023-53810 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'blk-mq release crypto keyslot ...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2023-53810',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 09 Dec 2025 01:16:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'blk-mq release crypto keyslot before reporting I/O complete\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Once all I/O using a blk_crypto_key has completed, filesystems can call\r\n' +
      "blk_crypto_evict_key().  However, the block layer currently doesn't call\r\n" +
      'blk_crypto_put_keyslot() until the request is being freed, which happens\r\n' +
      'after upper layers have been told (via bio_endio()) the I/O has\r\n' +
      'completed.  This causes a race condition where blk_crypto_evict_key()\r\n' +
      "can see 'slot_refs != 0' without there being an actual bug.\r\n" +
      '\r\n' +
      'This makes __blk_crypto_evict_key() hit the\r\n' +
      "'WARN_ON_ONCE(atomic_read(slot->slot_refs) != 0)' and return without\r\n" +
      'doing anything, eventually causing a use-after-free in\r\n' +
      'blk_crypto_reprogram_all_keys().  (This is a very rare bug and has only\r\n' +
      'been seen when per-file keys are being used with fscrypt.)\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'There are two options to fix this either release the keyslot before\r\n' +
      "bio_endio() is called on the request's last bio, or make\r\n" +
      "__blk_crypto_evict_key() ignore slot_refs.  Let's go with the first\r\n" +
      'solution, since it preserves the ability to report bugs (via\r\n' +
      'WARN_ON_ONCE) where a key is evicted while still in-use. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>',

    pubDate: 'Tue, 09 Dec 2025 01:16:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'ext4 fix rbtree traversal bug in ext4_mb_use_preallocated\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'During allocations, while looking for preallocations(PA) in the per\r\n' +
      "inode rbtree, we can't do a direct traversal of the tree because\r\n" +
      'ext4_mb_discard_group_preallocation() can paralelly mark the pa deleted\r\n' +
      'and that can cause direct traversal to skip some entries. This was\r\n' +
      'leading to a BUG_ON() being hit [1] when we missed a PA that could satisfy\r\n' +
      'our request and ultimately tried to create a new PA that would overlap\r\n' +
      'with the missed one.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'To makes sure we handle that case while still keeping the performance of\r\n' +
      'the rbtree, we make use of the fact that the only pa that could possibly\r\n' +
      'overlap the original goal start is the one that satisfies the below\r\n' +
      'conditions\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "  1. It must have it's logical start immediately to the left of\r\n" +
      '  (ie less than) original logical start.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '  2. It must not be deleted\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'To find this pa we use the following traversal method\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '1. Descend into the rbtree normally to find the immediate neighboring\r\n' +
      'PA. Here we keep descending irrespective of if the PA is deleted or if\r\n' +
      'it overlaps with our request etc. The goal is to find an immediately\r\n' +
      'adjacent PA.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '2. If the found PA is on right of original goal, use rb_prev() to find\r\n' +
      'the left adjacent PA.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '3. Check if this PA is deleted and keep moving left with rb_prev() until\r\n' +
      'a non deleted PA is found.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '4. This is the PA we are looking for. Now we can check if it can satisfy\r\n' +
      'the original request and proceed accordingly.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This approach also takes care of having deleted PAs in the tree.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '(While we are at it, also fix a possible overflow bug in calculating the\r\n' +
      'end of a PA)\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '[1] https//lore.kernel.org/linux-ext4/CA+G9fYv2FRpLqBZf34ZinR8bU2_ZRAUOjKAD3+tKRFaEQHtt8Q@mail.gmail.com/ | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>',
